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





What was implemented                                                          
                                                                                
  Task 1 — Prompt Templates (project/src/vlm/prompts/)                          
                                                                                
  ┌────────────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │          File          │                     Purpose                     │
  ├────────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ system_preamble.txt    │ Shared system prompt — environmental            │
  │                        │ psychologist persona + 5 strict rules           │
  ├────────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │                        │ Per-affordance prompt using string.Template     │
  │ user_template.txt      │ ($variable syntax) — injects detected objects,  │
  │                        │ few-shot block, and JSON schema                 │
  ├────────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │                        │ 2 calibrated examples per affordance (1         │
  │ few_shot_examples.json │ high-score ≥5, 1 low-score ≤2), with full       │
  │                        │ indicator JSON tailored to each affordance's    │
  │                        │ key cues                                        │
  └────────────────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  The template uses string.Template rather than str.format() — this avoids the
  {/} collision that would occur when Python's format parser encounters JSON
  curly braces inside the injected few-shot examples.

  Task 2 — run_vlm_annotation.py

  - Model loading: Qwen2VLForConditionalGeneration with device_map="auto",
  torch_dtype=torch.float16; processor configured with min/max pixel bounds
  - Batch loop: 300 images × 5 affordances = 1,500 pairs; skips completed pairs
  on restart
  - Prompt formatting: injects segmentation objects (or a fallback message if
  Agent 2 hasn't run yet), then few-shot examples
  - Inference: do_sample=False (greedy, equivalent to temperature=0.0),
  max_new_tokens=1024
  - Parsing: strips markdown fences, tries direct JSON parse, falls back to
  extracting the outermost {...} block
  - Validation: checks all required keys, score∈[1,7], confidence∈[0,1],
  non-empty indicators with valid type/polarity/strength
  - Retry: one retry with simplified prompt (no few-shot, terse JSON-only
  reminder)
  - Checkpointing: every 50 pairs; data/vlm_annotations/checkpoint.json
  - Progress: tqdm bar showing avg latency per pair and ETA

  Bonus — extract_indicator_vocab.py

  Post-run script that reads all raw annotation JSONs and produces:
  - indicator_vocabulary.json — per-affordance and cross-affordance term counts,
   majority-vote type/polarity, average strength
  - indicator_vocabulary_summary.txt — human-readable table

  ---
  Running on a GPU machine — full setup guide

  1. Prerequisites

  OS  : Ubuntu 20.04+ or similar Linux
  GPU : NVIDIA with ≥16 GB VRAM (RTX 3090 / A100 / A6000 / etc.)
  CUDA: 11.8 or 12.x  (check with: nvidia-smi)
  RAM : ≥32 GB system RAM recommended
  Disk: ≥50 GB free (model weights ~8 GB, images ~3 GB, outputs ~200 MB)

  2. Clone the repo

  git clone <your-repo-url>
  cd "COGS 185/FINAL/project"

  3. Python environment

  python3 -m venv .venv
  source .venv/bin/activate
  pip install --upgrade pip

  4. Install PyTorch (match your CUDA version)

  # CUDA 12.1 example — check https://pytorch.org/get-started for your version:
  pip install torch==2.3.0 torchvision==0.18.0 --index-url
  https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cu121

  5. Install AutoAWQ BEFORE transformers

  AutoAWQ must be installed first because it registers AWQ kernels that
  transformers then picks up:

  # Option A — pre-built wheel (fastest, CUDA 11.8/12.x):
  pip install autoawq

  # Option B — if the wheel doesn't match your CUDA:
  pip install git+https://github.com/casper-hansen/AutoAWQ.git

  6. Install remaining requirements

  pip install -r requirements.txt
  # Note: detectron2 is listed in requirements.txt as a manual install — only
  needed for
  # the segmentation pipeline (Agent 2), not for the VLM pipeline.

  7. Verify CUDA + model loading (optional smoke test)

  python3 -c "import torch; print('CUDA:', torch.cuda.is_available(),
  torch.cuda.get_device_name(0))"

  8. Log in to HuggingFace Hub (required for gated models)

  Qwen2-VL-7B-Instruct-AWQ is a public model but downloading large weights
  requires authentication:

  pip install huggingface_hub
  huggingface-cli login    # paste your HF token when prompted

  9. Transfer images

  If you're running on a remote GPU server, copy the images over:

  # From your local machine:
  rsync -avz "data/hypersim_pilot_420/"
  user@gpu-server:/path/to/project/data/hypersim_pilot_420/

  10. Dry-run to verify prompts

  python src/vlm/run_vlm_annotation.py \
      --image-dir data/hypersim_pilot_420 \
      --dry-run

  This prints the first 3 formatted prompts without loading the model. Confirm
  the few-shot block and detected objects section look correct.

  11. Run the full annotation pipeline

  python src/vlm/run_vlm_annotation.py \
      --image-dir data/hypersim_pilot_420 \
      --checkpoint-interval 50

  Useful flags:
  # Run only specific affordances (e.g. to parallelize across GPUs):
  --affordance-ids L079 L059

  # Smoke test — run only 10 pairs:
  --max-pairs 10

  # Resume after interruption (checkpoint is loaded automatically):
  # just re-run the same command — completed pairs are skipped

  Expected throughput: ~5–15 seconds/pair on an RTX 3090 → ~2–4 hours for all
  1,500 pairs.

  12. Extract indicator vocabulary

  After annotation is complete:

  python src/vlm/extract_indicator_vocab.py --min-count 2

  Outputs data/vlm_annotations/indicator_vocabulary.json and a human-readable
  summary.

  13. Output structure

  data/vlm_annotations/
  ├── raw/
  │   ├── ai_008_009_cam_00_frame0000_L059.json
  │   ├── ai_008_009_cam_00_frame0000_L079.json
  │   ├── ...  (1,500 files total)
  ├── checkpoint.json
  ├── indicator_vocabulary.json
  └── indicator_vocabulary_summary.txt











GPU Setup Guide — Windows / PowerShell / Driver 591.74
                                                                                
  Step 1 — Confirm your GPU has enough VRAM                       
                                                                                
  nvidia-smi                                                                    
                                                                                
  Look for your GPU name and VRAM. Qwen2-VL-7B-AWQ needs ≥10 GB VRAM (fp16 AWQ).
   16 GB recommended.                                             
                                                                                
  ---                                                             
  Step 2 — Install CUDA Toolkit 12.4
                                    
  Download and run the installer from NVIDIA:
  https://developer.nvidia.com/cuda-12-4-0-download-archive                     
  Select: Windows → x86_64 → 11 → exe (local)              
                                                                                
  After installation, verify:                                                   
  nvcc --version
  Expected: release 12.4                                                        
                                                                                
  ---
  Step 3 — Confirm Python and create virtual environment                        
                                                                                
  python --version   # should be 3.10–3.12
  cd "C:\path\to\COGS 185\FINAL\project"                                        
                                                                                
  python -m venv .venv                                                          
  .venv\Scripts\Activate.ps1                                                    
  python -m pip install --upgrade pip                                           
                                                                  
  If Activate.ps1 is blocked:                                                   
  Set-ExecutionPolicy -ExecutionPolicy RemoteSigned -Scope CurrentUser
  .venv\Scripts\Activate.ps1                                                    
                                                                  
  ---                                                                           
  Step 4 — Install PyTorch with CUDA 12.4
                                                                                
  pip install torch==2.5.1 torchvision==0.20.1 --index-url        
  https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cu124                                        
   
  Verify CUDA is visible to PyTorch:                                            
  python -c "import torch; print('CUDA:', torch.cuda.is_available()); 
  print('GPU:', torch.cuda.get_device_name(0))"                                 
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
  Step 5 — Install AutoAWQ (must come before transformers)                      
                                                                                
  AutoAWQ provides the quantisation kernels the AWQ model weights require:
                                                                                
  pip install autoawq                                             
                                                                                
  If the pre-built wheel fails (CUDA version mismatch), use the CUDA 12.4       
  specific wheel:
  pip install autoawq --extra-index-url https://huggingface.github.io/autoawq/  
                                                                  
  ---                                                                           
  Step 6 — Install the remaining requirements
                                                                                
  pip install -r requirements.txt                                 
                                                                                
  This installs transformers, qwen-vl-utils, accelerate, tqdm, pandas, Pillow,  
  etc.                                                                          
                                                                                
  detectron2 (for the segmentation pipeline) is not needed for VLM inference —  
  skip it for now.
                                                                                
  ---                                                             
  Step 7 — Log in to Hugging Face Hub
                                     
  The model weights (~8 GB) will be downloaded automatically on first run:      
                                                                                
  pip install huggingface_hub                                                   
  huggingface-cli login                                                         
                                                                                
  Paste your token from https://huggingface.co/settings/tokens when prompted.   
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
  Step 8 — Dry-run to verify prompts (no GPU needed)              
                                                                                
  python project\src\vlm\run_vlm_annotation.py --dry-run
                                                                                
  This prints the first 3 formatted prompts without loading the model. Confirm  
  the few-shot block, detected objects section, and affordance names look       
  correct.                                                                      
                                                                  
  ---
  Step 9 — Run the full annotation pipeline
                                                                                
  python project\src\vlm\run_vlm_annotation.py
                                                                                
  The script will:                                                              
  1. Download model weights on first run (one-time, ~8 GB to
  ~/.cache/huggingface/)                                                        
  2. Annotate all 2,100 pairs (420 images × 5 affordances)        
  3. Save one JSON per pair to data\vlm_annotations\raw\                        
  4. Checkpoint every 50 pairs — safe to Ctrl+C and resume                      
                                                                                
  Useful flags:                                                                 
  # Run only one affordance first as a sanity check:                            
  python src\vlm\run_vlm_annotation.py --affordance-ids L079 --max-pairs 5      
                                                                                
  # Restrict to specific affordances (e.g. to split work across sessions):      
  python src\vlm\run_vlm_annotation.py --affordance-ids L059 L079               
                                                                                
  # Resume after interruption (completed pairs are skipped automatically):      
  python src\vlm\run_vlm_annotation.py                                          
                                      
  Expected throughput: 5–20 seconds/pair depending on GPU. Full run ≈ 3–6 hours.
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
  Step 10 — Extract indicator vocabulary (after inference completes)            
                                                                                
  python src\vlm\extract_indicator_vocab.py --min-count 2
                                                                                
  Outputs:                                                                      
  - data\vlm_annotations\indicator_vocabulary.json                              
  - data\vlm_annotations\indicator_vocabulary_summary.txt                       
                                                                  
  ---                                                                           
  Troubleshooting quick reference                                 
                                                                                
  ┌───────────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │        Symptom        │                       Fix                       │
  ├───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤   
  │ CUDA not available    │ Reboot after CUDA Toolkit install; re-check     │
  │ after Step 4          │ with nvcc --version                             │   
  ├───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤   
  │ autoawq install fails │ Try pip install autoawq --no-build-isolation or │
  │                       │  install from source                            │   
  ├───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ qwen_vl_utils not     │ pip install qwen-vl-utils (underscore in        │   
  │ found                 │ import, hyphen in package name)                 │   
  ├───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ OutOfMemoryError on   │ Your VRAM may be under 10 GB; try adding        │   
  │ GPU                   │ --affordance-ids L059 to run one at a time      │   
  ├───────────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ source is not         │ You're in PowerShell — use                      │   
  │ recognised            │ .venv\Scripts\Activate.ps1                      │   
  └───────────────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                                                                                
✻ Brewed for 58s                                                  

❯ Error in step 4: could not install packages due to an OSError: INvalid URL    
'https:/download.pytorch.org/wh1/cu124/torchvision/': No host supplied          
                                                                                
⏺ The URL got corrupted when copying — two characters are wrong: https:/        
  (missing a slash) and wh1 (that's a 1, not an l). Type this manually or copy
  carefully:                                                                    
   
  pip install torch==2.5.1 torchvision==0.20.1 --index-url                      
  https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cu124                                        
                                                                                
  The two fixes:                                                                
  - https:// — two forward slashes                                
  - whl — ends in a lowercase letter l, not the number 1
